## Eat

When it comes to eating options, you're spoiled for choice in Xiamen. See
for a general Fujianese menu reader.

### Budget food areas

Two areas with many cheap local restaurants are around the university and the many smaller streets near Zhongshan Rd, inland from the ferry terminus.

There is an old restaurant on the east end of Zhongshan Rd (intersection of Xinhua Rd) which serves the local dish Shachamian, noodles with peanut soup.
also has much cheap food, though prices there are higher than Xiamen.

### Around the lake

The area from the north side of Yundang Lake over to Haiwan Park has a large number of bars, cafes and restaurants. Most are mid-to-high priced, though there are exceptions. Many are popular with Xiamen's large community of expatriates.

There is a whole strip of about twenty cafes and bars along the lake on
(西堤咖啡一条街) running West from the Marco Polo Hotel. Most of them are in villa-style homes converted to cafes with patios or balconies with a view of the lake; these are upmarket establishments whose clients include tourists and expats, but are mainly well-off locals. The parking area along the lake always has many BMWs, Audis and SUVs, and often a Ferrari or two.
Most of these serve Western food, but many have Chinese dishes as well and there are some with other specialties. The area also has some stores, also mostly upmarket, selling things like ceramics and lacquerwork.

#### Coyote Cafe & Cantina

Tex-Mex food made with fresh ingredients. Excellent cheesecake. 58-2 Ganglong Huayuan Off the main road east of Marco Polo, right down on the lake shore


#### Geo Geo Cafe

Serves good Italian and American food and coffee. No. 3, Yundang Road (Xidi Coffee Street) on the corner a block west of Marco Polo

#### Tuscany Cafe

Mainly European dishes with a few Mexican dishes. The owner/chef is a former chef of the Four Seaons Hotel, Hong Kong. The prices are reasonable, with most items under ¥50 with free bruschetta. They also have a special lunch menu which is quite cheap. The staff are able to speak English. 厦门市湖滨北路27号海湾新城102之二 Shop 102-2

Greg's is a little piece of France in China. They serve traditional French dishes, from bouillabaisse to the lamb shank, including Gillardeau oysters from Arcachon. The chef adapts his recipes for each customer, personalising the sauce and way of cooking. He also changes the menu seasonally, featuring fresh seasonal products. 1C N 10 Hubin Bei Road

in Chinese), just west of the lake, also has a number of places:

### Around the university

Xiada Street, between the university main gate and Nanputuo Temple, has many restaurants. These mainly cater to the student trade, so they tend to be relatively plain but to offer good value. Neither English menus nor English-speaking staff are common.

Along the boardwalk by the beach, from near the university out toward Hulishan Fortress, are many more restaurants and food stalls.

Offers excellent Chinese food, mainly spicy Sichuan food, at an affordable price. There is English on the menu, but staff do not speak English. Xiao La Jiao Xiahe Commercial Building (厦禾商厦), No.323, Xiahe Rd


## Drink

As everywhere in China, there are many tea houses in Xiamen and many KTVs (the 'K' is for Karaoke); both are quite popular with locals. See
for background information. A local speciality is
(工夫茶), a type of black tea that is also popular in
and in
.

Xiamen also has many bars and discos in a more-or-less western style; these are generally more affordable than comparable places in Shanghai or Beijing. Although crowded, these places are generally safe. Some caution is required, however, since
sometimes take advantage of the crowding and drunken customers sometimes get combative.

#### 1801 Bar

A disco with mainly R&B and hip-hop music. Open well into the small hours, sometimes past dawn. 1st floor of the United Hotel, Hubin Bei Lu (Lakeside South Road)


#### Dushang bar

Loud and expensive, but popular and lively. 湖滨东路188号1楼 No.1 Building, No.188 Hubin Dong Lu (Lakeside East Street)


#### The Key

Live music from a Filipino cover band with a broad repertoire — jazz and latin as well as rock and hip hop. 湖滨西路海湾公园109号 109 Hubin Xilu (Lakeside West Street) Haiwan Park, on the inland side


#### KK Disco Pub

in Haiwan Park, near the Key

Also, most of the major hotels have live music from Filipino cover bands in their bars.

Alternative and cheaper nightlife can be found in Zengcuo An, formerly a separate village now a neighborhood near Xiamen University. Here you find a lot of cheap pubs, open-air BBQ´s and casual gatherings of students and other young people who enjoy the sunset and mild Xiamen nights over a drink.

#### Temple Cafe

Coffee, beer and cocktails in a unique location, in the courtyard of a functioning Buddhist temple. Western menu, moderate prices. No. 61 Zengcuo An, Siming District

That area also has many hotels, mostly small and moderately priced.

## Sleep

This lists accommodation on Xiamen Island only. Staying in
instead might save a little money and could be reasonably convenient if you choose a place near a BRT stop. There is also plenty of accommodation on

### Budget


#### Xiamen Old Town Hostel

A family-run hostel in a three-floor house located in one of the oldest parts of Xiamen, very central. The hostel has a large rooftop garden with a view of the city and harbour, wireless Internet, and big community kitchen. It is right off of the Kaihe road food market, one of the largest open air markets in China with lots of fresh veggies and seafood. You can also eat some of the cheapest food in China at many small local eateries. 厦门古街青年旅舍 Kaihe Road, 24 Jiutiao alley (开禾路-九条巷24) from Train Station take the BRT in front of the station #3/#2/#1 exit at Kaihe Road stop (开禾路). The hostel is a little hard to find, deep in a maze of narrow alleys, but the neighbors seem to know that travelers are looking for this place. From the airport it is best to take a taxi to intersection of Xiahe road (厦禾路) and Kaihe Road (开禾路). From there, call the hostel and staff will come find you.


#### Hostel Locanda

One block from the waterfront with Gulangyu island across the water. It is a 10-minute walk to Zhongshan Road and Lundu Ferry and 20-minute walk to Xiamen University. Lovely double rooms upstairs, but the dorms on the ground floor are cramped and the shared bathrooms far from clean. Garden but no kitchen at all. No.35 Minzu Rd, Siming District


#### Xiamen Baijiacun International Youth Hostel

Clean, spacious hostel in a great location at Zhongshan Gongyuan (中山公园). 厦门百家村国际青年旅舍 20 Liaohua Lu (蓼花路20) from Songbo (松柏) bus station, take bus #86/#616 to Gongyuan Dong Lu (公园东路), the hostel is on the opposite side with a red wall, taxi ¥17


#### Xiamen International Youth Hostel

Very well kept YHA hostel, dorms or rooms are impeccably clean and comfortable. Friendly, small kitchen, bar, space to sit. Close to Xiamen university and easily reached by bus (1 or 21 from the railway station, ¥1). 41 Nanhua Road, Siming District


#### Meihulu Hotel

Small place that accepts foreign passports and is quiet, yet conveniently located. From ¥70. 美湖鹭酒店 52-5 Hubin Nan Lu (湖滨南路52-5号), Siming District Almost invisible on the opposite left of the long-distance bus station


#### Xiamen Travellers' Home

A very homy place to stay for holiday. clean, great hospitality, 5 rooms ensure small number of guests staying. 旅行者之家 No.23 Zeng Cuo An, Island Ring Road 厦门环岛路曾厝垵23号


### Mid-range


#### Gem Hotel

Beautiful Japanese-style rooms overlooking much of downtown Xiamen. Includes Chinese buffet breakfast and free wired internet access. Most of the staff speak English well and are extremely helpful.


#### Jing Hua Hotel

Three-star hotel offering 146 air-conditioned rooms, all of which have Internet access, satellite TV, and mini-bar. Some of its amenities include KTV, fitness center, and sauna. 1130 Xiahe Rd, Siming District


#### Lujiang Harbourview Hotel

The closest thing Xiamen has to a Grand Old Hotel, it was founded by the famed local tycoon and philanthropist Tan Kah Kee in 1958, and built in a unique fusion of traditional European and Chinese architectural styles that was pioneered by Tan Kah Kee himself, which can also be seen in other buildings whose construction he funded in both Xiamen and Singapore. 54 Lujiang Rd 100 metres south of the ferry station, at the foot of Zhongshan Road


#### Somerset Software Park Xiamen

With 167 apartments ranging from studio to three bedroom apartments, the property is equipped with a breakfast lounge, children's playground, gymnasium and a video room. No.2 Jinshan Rd, Siming District


### Splurge


#### Le Méridien Xiamen

Surrounded by open spaces and lush vegetation. Nestled on a slope of Xianyue Hill. Breathtaking views of Xiamen Bay. 厦门艾美酒店 7 Guanjun Rd


#### Marco Polo Hotel

This hotel is on Yundang Lake, and offers a very good international buffet and a great atmosphere.


#### Millennium Harbourview Hotel Xiamen

Located in downtown Xiamen which is a major shopping and business district, the hotel is only minutes away on foot to the ferry to Gulangyu Island. It features a 22-story building that houses 352 rooms that include various business facilities including a work-desk and high speed Internet access. 12-8 Zhenhai Rd


#### Pan Pacific Xiamen

A super modern hotel with stunning sea views and natural scenery. The rooms use a lot of glass and modern design techniques. The hotel also has an excellent ¥100 lunch buffet. Facilities include a fitness center, spa and pool. 19 Hubin Bei Lu (Lakeside North Road)


#### Sheraton Xiamen Hotel

The latest international chain hotel to grace Xiamen's shores. It is very plush, and the Waves Pan Asian buffet is very good. 386-1 Jiahe Rd


#### Xiamen Fliport Software Park Hotel

Luxury hotel in a software park development area near the airport


## Connect

#### Philippines

No. 2 Ling Xiang Li, Lianhua District

#### Thailand

Visa section open only 09:00-11:30. Building No.3 (City Hotel Xiamen), No. 16 Hu Yuan Road

above, Xiamen has a number of smaller stores catering to expat residents.

The most comprehensive collection of western supermarket items including a good selection of international beers. 10-105 Jianye Rd near the Marco Polo

4 天罗马城市微度假（Mid-range Budget，≈ 150–200 €/天含住宿）

────────────────
1. 行前速览
• 最佳交通票：48 h/72 h Roma Pass（含 1–2 个景点免排队＋公交地铁通票）或单纯买 BIT 100 min 票（1.5 €）＋单次地铁票（1.5 €）。  
• 住宿：Termini 车站周边 3 星或精品 B&B，双人间 90–120 €/晚；Trastevere 或 Prati 区稍贵但夜生活丰富。  
• 预算拆分：住宿 100 €、餐饮 50 €、门票交通 30 €、杂项 20 €。  
• 餐厅定位：人均 15–25 €午餐、25–35 €晚餐，含一杯酒。

────────────────
2. 4 日行程（含美食节点）

DAY 1｜古城核心  
上午  
08:00 斗兽场（提前官网订 9:00 时段门票 18 €）→ 帕拉蒂尼山 & 古罗马广场（联票）  
午餐  
12:30 Pizzeria Ai Marmi（Trastevere，罗马薄底披萨 8–10 €）  
下午  
14:30 卡比托利欧山 & 威尼斯广场（步行 10 min）  
16:00 纳沃纳广场 & 万神殿（免费）  
晚餐  
19:30 Da Francesco（纳沃纳旁，Carbonara 12 €，需排队）  
夜行  
21:30 特雷维喷泉夜景 → 回酒店地铁 A 线 Barberini 站

DAY 2｜梵蒂冈 & 河右岸  
上午  
08:00 梵蒂冈博物馆（预约 8:30 入场 17 €）→ 西斯廷礼拜堂  
12:00 圣彼得大教堂（免费，登顶圆顶 10 €）  
午餐  
13:30 Pizzarium Bonci（梵蒂冈北口外，切块披萨按重量 15 €）  
下午  
15:00 圣天使堡（14 €）→ 漫步圣天使桥  
17:00 台伯河右岸跳蚤市场（Porta Portese 周日才有，平日可改去 Via dei Coronari 古董街）  
晚餐  
19:30 Il Sorpasso（Prati 区，冷切拼盘＋手工面 25 €）  
夜行  
21:00 Trastevere 小酒馆（Freni e Frizioni，鸡尾酒 8 €）

DAY 3｜巴洛克 & 咖啡  
上午  
08:30 西班牙阶梯 → 康多蒂街咖啡站 Sant’Eustachio Il Caffè（拿铁 2.2 €）  
10:00 波各赛美术馆（需提前订 13 €，两小时限流）

下午  
15:00 人民广场 → 步行至 Villa Borghese 公园野餐  
17:00 地铁 B 线到 Circo Massimo → 帕拉蒂尼山日落  
晚餐  
19:30 Flavio al Velavevodetto（Testaccio，炖牛尾 18 €）  
夜行  
22:00 Testaccio 夜店（Akab 或 L’Alibi，入场 10–15 €）

DAY 4｜城南 & 本地市场  
上午  
08:30 地铁 B 线到 Circo Massimo → 阿文提诺山橙园（免费钥匙孔看圣彼得）  
10:00 卡拉卡拉浴场（13 €）  
午餐  
12:30 Mercato Testaccio 熟食摊（Mordi & Vai 牛尾包 6 €）  
下午  
14:00 Eataly Ostiense（逛超市＋屋顶啤酒 5 €）  
16:00 回酒店取行李 → Leonardo Express 机场快线 32 min 14 €

────────────────
3. 交通细节
• 机场往返：  
  – Leonardo Express 直达 Termini 14 €，30 min；  
  – SIT 或 Terravision 巴士 6 €，50 min。  
• 市内：  
  – 地铁 A/B/C 线＋有轨电车 3、8 号线覆盖 90 % 景点；  
  – 步行古城核心区最省时，Google Map 预估时间＋20 % 爬坡。  
• 打车：起步 6 €，夜间/行李附加，Uber 仅 Uber Black 较贵。

────────────────
4. 美食备忘
• 必吃清单：  
  – Carbonara（奶酪蛋酱面）  
  – Cacio e Pepe（奶酪胡椒面）  
  – Supplì（炸饭团）  
  – Maritozzo（奶油甜面包）  
  – Gelato：Giolitti 或 Fatamorgana  
• 订位：除高端餐厅外，多数小馆不接受订位，19:00 前到可少排队。  
• 小费：账单已含 Coperto 或 Servizio，无需额外 10 %，可留 1–2 € 硬币。

────────────────
5. 预算速算（4 天 3 夜）
住宿 300 €  
餐饮 200 €  
门票/交通 120 €  
杂项 80 €  
合计 ≈ 700 €/人

────────────────
6. 不确定信息
• 2024 年罗马市政府可能调整地铁票价，建议出行前再查 ATAC 官网确认。  
• 个别小馆营业时间随季节变动，若遇关门可现场用 TheFork 或 Google 即时搜索附近备选。

祝旅途愉快，Buon viaggio!

用户问题: what can I buy in hangzhou

相关指南信息:

==================================================【指南 1】 Hangzhou > Buy | 分类: Shopping
## Buy  
on Tiyuchang Road. You can also get silk at other places in the city, but most of it will just be the fabric. It is open from 08:00-17:00 and is near the Zhejiang International Hotel.
hard!
(夜市) off Yan'an Road near Pinghai Road (right near Wushan) every night. Here you can find Mao memorabilia, jewellery, paper fans, pipes, luggage, handicrafts and other items that most Chinese cities have. Pirated DVDs and counterfeit handbags are for sale as well. You can also find a lot of those silk-screen printed paintings/embroidery things that the silk market also has. Bargain very hard - Many stalls sell the same stuff, so be prepared to walk away. Be careful buying "antiques" because they are probably new, and pearls. Often the pearl culturing process has been very short, and in fact the "pearl" is a plastic marble with only the thinnest of cultured skin.
(电子产品市场 - Running west-east in north-west Hangzhou on Wensan Road are several indoor, multistory electronics shopping centers offering all manner of electronics including desktop computers, laptops, computer software (licensed and un-licensed), cellphones, mp3 players, and hundreds of peripherals and storage media. Pirated DVDs and computer games are offered as well, and if you are obviously a foreigner, vendors will shout "DVD! DVD!" at you to urge you to browse their selection.
- Several in town, Gucui Rd and Wener West Rd in the west, another on Jichang Rd in north, the interesting one is next to Wushan Square, downtown. On 3 or 4 floors, this market is stuffed with pets and plants. Also sections selling Traditional Chinese Medicine (TCM), with dried snake and seahorse, huge dried mushrooms and other strange things.
- Dragon Well/Longjing tea is famous throughout China and worth getting if you like green tea. If you are staying with a Chinese host somewhere else in China after Hangzhou, bringing them a small box (or two) of higher-end Longjing Tea would make a great gift; however, these usually cost around ¥300/box (more at tourist stands). The Longjing village and tea fields area of Hangzhou (southwest of West Lake) are where Longjing tea is grown. Besides being worth a visit for the scenic sights alone, tea can be purchased here as well - fresh from the harvesters' bags if so desired. Many places across the city also sell tea, such as informal vendors and small shops easily identifiable by the boxes displayed inside or store names such as "西湖龙井茶" (West Lake Dragon Well Tea), as well as grocery stores and supermarket chains. Because of the fame of Longjing tea, fake and low-grade varieties exist. If you have no experience buying tea, purchase from a reputable-looking establishment or ask the advise of a knowledgeable native.
- Hangzhou has literally hundreds of clothes and shoes stores. The largest concentration of these are on Yan'an Rd and especially Wulin Rd, making a straight line of clothes shops stacked on top of each other between Wushan and Wulin Squares. Another popular clothing spot is "Song Mu Chang" (松木场) just north of the lake on Shuguang Road. All of these places require bargaining and often have a lot of fake ripoff clothes. For the real thing, try the department stores (i.e. Hangzhou Tower across between Yan'an and Nanshan Roads). You can certainly find cheaper clothes stores scattered throughout the city as you get farther from the lake if you really like to buy clothes.
- There are several places to buy Chinese landscape paintings in the city, especially near Wushan Square and around the south/east side of the lake.
has a supermarket in the downtown area east of West Lake (on South Yan'an Lu). In addition its large selection of groceries, it carries a wider variety of Western foods such as cheeses and breads than most other grocery stores in the city. What this really means is a single aisle of Western brands and foods. Do not expect a large selection. This is also a good place to purchase western liquor. French Gin is as little as ¥55 per litre, Captain Morgan rum about ¥75 and Cointreau ¥135. How these prices are about half of duty free escapes this contributor.
(好又多) is a superstore chain Westerners may recognize as being similar to Wal-Mart. It's in the shopping center near the Yellow Dragon Sports Stadium north of West Lake and the Baochu Pagoda area, and has a large grocery section that boasts fresh meats, seafood, and produce as well as the normal selection of packaged food.
of all prices and qualities are available from bike shops scattered across Hangzhou. Bargaining is necessary at all but large chain stores, and generally one gets what he or she pays for (the cheapest bikes will begin to rust and break quickly). The indoor
near the corner of Wener and Xueyuan Lu offers a huge assortment of electric bikes/scooters and batteries, and Trust-Mart (see above) also has a reasonable selection of bicycles and a small selection of electric bikes/scooters. Any bike, regardless of the value, will be stolen if left unattended and unsecured. Be sure to buy at least one lock (two for expensive scooters and bikes) to protect your purchase. Scooters may also require a locking frame to guard the battery from theft. A cycling club based in Hangzhou.
the MIXC mall located next to the Qintang River in the new Central Business District has an enormous collection of high-end luxury brands including LV, Armani, Ferragamo and the like, but also has Hangzhou's best market for imported foods. "Ole" is located in the B2 level of the mall and be prepared to spend big. The cinema complex on the 3rd, 4th and 5th levels has 12 screens including the largest of the two IMAX theatre's in the city. Also on the 4th floor is a full Olympic size ice skating arena open daily from 10:30-22:00. Ticket prices range from ¥50 for unlimited skating time on regular weekdays (¥60 after 17:30) and ¥70 for 2 hour sessions on weekends and holiday. Price includes new Canadian rental skates, use of free locker and all safety gear (elbows, wrist and knee protectors and use of helmets). The rink is modern, clean and well trained and friendly professional staff. The skating school is reasonably priced and geared entirely for beginners. The 30m x 60m ice is resurfaced every 2 hours by a Zamboni machine.
The
at the center of Hangzhou, the Yanan road. The first floor is the cosmetics selling floor. From floor two to floor six are all clothes selling stores. Floor two sells fashionable brands.

【指南 2】 Liuzhou > Buy | 分类: Shopping
## Buy  
. Miniature souvenir coffins. From the Chinese saying "Be born in Suzhou, live in Hangzhou, eat in Guangzhou and die in Liuzhou." Liuzhou used to be famous for its coffins which were made from the local high quality wood. Today, only miniature versions are available and are popular as good luck charms as the Chinese for coffin can be used as a play on words for "Gain Promotion and Increase Wealth"

【指南 3】 Plitvice Lakes National Park > Buy | 分类: Shopping
## Buy  
Numerous souvenir shops can be found near the entrances of the park. Caution is advised however, as many overpriced souvenirs sold as "authentic hand crafts" from Croatia are made in China.

【指南 4】 Hangzhou | 分类: Others
# Hangzhou
> Hierarchy: Asia > East Asia > China > East China > Zhejiang > Hangzhou  
(杭州;
in Wu,
in Mandarin) is the capital of
province. It is one of the most important tourist cities in China, famous for its natural beauty and historical and cultural heritage.  
Hangzhou serves as the political, economic, and cultural center of Zhejiang province. It is a prosperous and highly developed city that attracts many migrants from less affluent provinces seeking employment opportunities. The city experiences high humidity during the summer months, from early June to early September. It has also emerged as a secondary tech hub for China, being home to the corporate headquarters of Chinese e-commerce giant Alibaba and its founder Jack Ma.

【指南 6】 Yueyang > Buy | 分类: Shopping
## Buy  
Yueyang offers a variety of local specialties and souvenirs that make for perfect gifts and mementos.
(君山银针) - This is a high-quality yellow tea produced on Junshan Island in Dongting Lake. It is known for its unique appearance and mild flavor.
(洞庭碧螺春) - A type of green tea known for its delicate spiral shape and floral aroma.
- Small models of the iconic Yueyang Tower are popular souvenirs.
(湘绣) - As one of China's four famous embroideries, Xiangxiu is renowned for its intricate designs and vibrant colors. You can find embroidered items like handkerchiefs and wall hangings.
(洞庭银鱼) - These small, white, dried fish are a local delicacy. They are often used in soups or stir-fried with eggs.  
For shopping, you can find these items at:
- Convenient but prices might be higher.
- For a wider selection of teas.
- A bustling street near the Yueyang Tower scenic area with various shops and stalls selling souvenirs and snacks .

【输出 / 解答】:
在杭州，你可以买到以下特色商品和纪念品：

1. 丝绸：Tiyuchang Road 的丝绸市场（08:00-17:00，靠近浙江国际大酒店）是首选，其他地方大多只卖布料。  
2. 龙井茶：最著名的绿茶，可在龙井村或市区标有“西湖龙井茶”的店铺购买，注意辨别真假。  
3. 夜市小商品：延安路靠近平海路的夜市每晚都有，可淘到毛主席纪念品、首饰、纸扇、手工艺品、盗版DVD、仿名牌包、丝网印刷画等，记得狠狠砍价。  
4. 电子产品：文三路一带有多层电子商城，卖电脑、手机、MP3、配件及盗版软件/DVD。  
5. 花鸟与中药材：吴山广场旁的市场有宠物、植物、中药材（干蛇、海马、大蘑菇等）。  
6. 服饰鞋包：延安路、武林路、松木场（曙光路北）店铺林立，需砍价；想买正品可去百货商场如杭州大厦。  
7. 中国画：吴山广场及湖东南侧一带可购中国山水画。  
8. 日用品/进口食品：  
   - 家乐福（延安南路）有西式奶酪、面包、洋酒。  
   - 好又多（黄龙体育中心附近）类似沃尔玛，生鲜、日用品齐全。  
9. 奢侈品：万象城（钱塘江边CBD）汇聚LV、Armani等高端品牌，地下“Ole”超市专卖进口食品。  
10. 自行车/电动车：市区多家店可买，文二路与学院路交汇处的市场电动车品种多；记得加锁防盗。

总之，从丝绸、龙井茶到夜市小玩意、电子产品、服饰、画作乃至奢侈品，杭州都能满足你的购物需求。

以下回答基于我的已有知识，而非检索到的 Wikivoyage 页面。

杭州 48 小时精华推荐  
1. 西湖环湖步行＋骑行：断桥残雪—白堤—孤山—西泠印社—楼外楼午餐—苏堤—花港观鱼，傍晚雷峰塔看日落。理由：一天把经典湖景、人文、美食一次打包。  
2. 灵隐寺 & 飞来峰：早 7:30 前进景区避开人潮，飞来峰石刻＋永福寺素面。理由：佛教圣地＋石窟艺术，清晨最清净。  
3. 龙井村茶田徒步：从“龙井八景”牌坊走到狮峰山，找茶农试喝明前龙井。理由：看茶园、学采茶、买茶不踩坑。  
4. 西溪湿地摇橹船：周家村入口，2 小时水路看芦苇、水鸟。理由：城市绿肺，四季皆美，船比步行省力。  
5. 河坊街＋南宋御街夜游：吃葱包桧、定胜糕，看胡庆余堂中药博物馆夜景。理由：老杭州烟火气，夜景拍照出片。  
6. 中国茶叶博物馆双峰馆区：人少、建筑美，免费盖章。理由：深度了解龙井与茶道，雨天好去处。  
7. 杭州国家版本馆（文润阁）：2022 年新开放，建筑大师王澍作品，需预约。理由：现代宋韵＋国宝级典籍，拍照极美。  
8. 千岛湖一日游（可选）：高铁至淳安 30 min，乘游艇登梅峰岛俯瞰 1078 个岛屿。理由：水质一级棒，鱼头汤必吃。  

吃  
- 楼外楼：西湖醋鱼、宋嫂鱼羹，临湖座位需等位。  
- 知味观（湖滨总店）：小笼、猫耳朵，当早餐不排队。  
- 福缘居：杭帮菜新派，醉蟹、东坡肉，环境好。  
- 青芝坞/白沙泉：咖啡、精酿、私房菜集中，夜生活新据点。  

住  
- 西子湖四季：湖景房自带私家码头，预算充足首选。  
- 西湖国宾馆：毛泽东住过的 1 号楼，园林私密。  
- 桔子水晶（西湖店）：性价比高，步行 5 min 到地铁龙翔桥。  

行  
- 地铁 1、3 号线覆盖主要景点，支付宝领“杭州地铁乘车码”。  
- 共享单车遍地，西湖边有电子围栏，记得定点还车。  
- 打车高峰极堵，建议地铁＋步行组合。  

不确定信息  
- 2024 年西湖音乐喷泉是否恢复夜间演出，建议抵达后现场确认。  
- 灵隐寺香花券价格可能随季节调整，以景区当日公示为准。

用户问题: give me someplace to visit near chinatown singapore

回答:

------------------------------
【输出 / 解答】:
以下回答基于我的已有知识，而非检索到的 Wikivoyage 页面。

如果你人在新加坡牛车水（Chinatown）附近，想顺路再逛一两个点，下面 4 个地方走路 5–15 分钟就能到，且各有特色，可按兴趣挑选：

1. 佛牙寺龙华院（Buddha Tooth Relic Temple & Museum）  
   就在牛车水中心，外观金碧辉煌，内部供奉佛牙舍利。免费入场，每天 09:00–18:00 开放，顶楼空中花园和地宫都值得一看。建议上午去，人少、光线好，拍照更出片。

2. 麦士威熟食中心（Maxwell Food Centre）  
   从佛牙寺后门步行 3 分钟即到。想吃地道本地味，直接排队：  
   • 天天海南鸡饭（11:00 前到，否则卖完）  
   • 真真粥品（鱼片粥、猪杂粥）  
   • 老伴豆花（当甜品，口感像布丁）  
   记得带现金，大部分摊位不收电子支付。

3. 安详山（Ann Siang Hill）／客纳街（Club Street）  
   从牛车水地铁站 Exit A 出来，沿 Ann Siang Road 上坡 5 分钟即到。这一带是旧店屋改造的酒吧、咖啡馆和独立买手店集中地。白天逛店拍照，晚上 18:00 以后整条街变露天酒吧区，周五周六最热闹。不确定哪家好喝，就选人气旺的「The Old Man Singapore」或「Operation Dagger」。

4. 新加坡城市美术馆（Singapore City Gallery）  
   位于牛车水边缘的 Maxwell Road，走路约 10 分钟。免费入场，有 1:400 的巨型市区模型和互动沙盘，能快速了解新加坡城市规划和未来项目。冷气足，适合中午避暑。周一闭馆，其余时间 09:00–17:00 开放。

交通小贴士  
• 地铁：牛车水站 NE4/DT19 是枢纽，去哪都方便。  
• 步行：上述地点彼此距离 1 km 内，穿双舒适鞋即可。  
• 打车：Grab/Gojek 在牛车水容易叫到，但高峰时段（17:30–19:30）可能堵车，建议地铁或步行。

不确定你偏好美食、文化还是夜生活，但以上 4 点基本覆盖，可按时间自由组合。祝旅途愉快！

Yes—if you’re in San Francisco’s Chinatown, you’ll find two bars right in the neighborhood:

The guides don’t list any bars specifically inside Boston’s, Milan’s, The Hague’s, or Suwon’s Chinatowns, so these two are the only confirmed options.
